  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1581685-does-sabrina-s-character-improve">Does Sabrina&#39;s character improve throughout these books? Right now I can&#39;t stand her, and it&#39;s only gotten worse since the first book. It kind of sucks having a main character who is such a arrogant, selfish, and self-righteous brat because even though I like Daphne, Granny, Canis, Puck (love him), and the others, Sabrina is so bad that I&#39;m about to quit reading the series.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1581685'><a id="like_count_community_question_1581685" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1581685?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F112879.Once_Upon_a_Crime">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/70143236-julie"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1603157513i/70143236._UY100_CR38,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/70143236-julie">julie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I understand your feelings towards Sabrina. She is arrogant, selfish, and self-righteous, and is bigoted towards her fairy-tale town for a long time b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I understand your feelings towards Sabrina. She is arrogant, selfish, and self-righteous, and is bigoted towards her fairy-tale town for a long time because of the pain they brought upon her and her family. However, I do think Sabrina improves, however slowly, throughout the books. She begins to realize the good that the characters have done and continue to do for her, and also realizes she needs to be kinder and more understanding. Sabrina still has fits of her bad qualities, but it makes her more real. I wouldn't stop reading the series because of her annoying qualities, however, because the series is awesome and Sabrina does realize her selfish nature and attempts to fix it. What I remember is that all of her bad qualities come from fear and a need to protect her family, which makes sense. Sorry that this was so long!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_271160040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271160040" />
    <a title="Bridgette Redman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7011555-bridgette-redman"><img alt="Bridgette Redman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328158182p2/7011555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271160040?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bridgette Redman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bridgette Redman" href="/user/show/7011555-bridgette-redman">Bridgette Redman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271160040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5095881841298918913">The Sisters Grimm never fails to amuse because of the way it takes famous fairy-related literature and puts a modern twist on them. Far more than the overall plot or even the themes, it is the little moments in these books that make them worthy reads. <br/><br/>Once Upon a Crime is the fourth adventure of Sabrina and Daphne Grimm, two children who late discovered their family heritage as the jailer and protector of fairy tale creatures known as Everafters. After spending months in an orphanage and one lou</span>
  <span id="freeText5095881841298918913" style="display:none">The Sisters Grimm never fails to amuse because of the way it takes famous fairy-related literature and puts a modern twist on them. Far more than the overall plot or even the themes, it is the little moments in these books that make them worthy reads. <br /><br />Once Upon a Crime is the fourth adventure of Sabrina and Daphne Grimm, two children who late discovered their family heritage as the jailer and protector of fairy tale creatures known as Everafters. After spending months in an orphanage and one lousy foster home after another, they were told they had a grandmother—a woman they thought was dead. They go to live with her in Ferry Port Landing, which they soon learn is home to most of the fairy tale creatures they've read about. However, all of these Everafters are trapped in Ferry Port Landing for as long as one of the Grimms are alive. This makes them a less than popular twosome. <br /><br />After several adventures where they solve mysteries and help save Ferry Port Landing, they make their first trip out. In the previous adventure The Problem Child, their Grandmother's ward, Puck, was injured and is in a coma. The only thing likely to save him is to get him back to the Fairy land where his parents reign. Much to Sabrina's disgust, this is in New York City, a place she associates with home and a complete lack of Everafters. <br /><br />While Daphne has been thrilled to take on the job of fairy tale detective, Sabrina still resists. She hates their calling and wants nothing to do with it. She decides the trip to New York will be her final case. She can then concentrate on saving her parents—who are in a magical sleep that no one can wake them from—and return to her normal life. <br /><br />What she discovers instead is that her seemingly normal mother was highly active in the fairy community in New York City and unlike the attitude that Ferry Port Everafters have toward the Grimms, the New York City Everafters honor and adore them. <br /><br />In Once Upon a Crime, you learn a little more about Puck’s family. His story, obviously, comes from William Shakespeare's A Midsummer Night's Dream and it is in this book that you get to meet the rest of the fairy creatures from the famous play. It's one of the things that will delight any lover of classical literature. It's also what gave the book its greatest appeal to my 10-year-old son who has seen the play numerous times since he was five. Puck is also a great favorite of his as it is his final two speeches that were the first he ever memorized. His view of Puck isn't far off from the Puck that is met in The Sisters Grimm—an 11-year-old boy who sees himself as a villain despite his golden heart. <br /><br />While Shakespeare doesn't claim it, author Michael Buckley tells us that Puck is the offspring of Oberon and Titania, a fairy prince who was promised to one of the other fairies. Titania's fairy attendants get much greater play in this novel, with fleshed out personalities and goals. <br /><br />At its heart Once Upon a Crime is a classic mystery story despite being populated with fantastical creatures. It also continues to expose the growing pains that Sabrina is having as she must make a choice between selfishness and service and discover what it really means to be a family. <br /><br />Sabrina is frequently a frustrating character despite being the protagonist because she is so distrustful and resists the route that others—and the readers—want her to go. Nothing ever comes easy for her, but mostly because she insists upon making it difficult. Is this really any surprise when we realize we're talking about a pre-teen girl on the cusp of puberty? <br /><br />Michael Buckley continues to entertain with The Sisters Grimm series. Each offering in the series changes the characters in subtle and not-so-subtle ways. The books are quick reads and I look forward to each new book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5095881841298918913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The Grimm sisters find out that they are the descendants of the famed Brothers Grimm, who brought the fairy tale creatures </span>
  <span id="freeText3827996963036786907" style="display:none">The Sisters Grimm series are my audiobook standbys. The narrator is fantastic and these are perfect for long drives in the car. The series is about two young girls, Daphne and Sabrina, who, after the disappearance of their parents and a year spent jumping from one wretched foster home to another, go to live with the grandmother they never knew they had in Fairyport Landing. The Grimm sisters find out that they are the descendants of the famed Brothers Grimm, who brought the fairy tale creatures over to live in Fairyport landing. The fun part is, it's not just Grimm's fairy tales that show up in the book. Puck from Midsummer Night's Dream, the Wizard of Oz, and Mother Goose all appear. The sisters, their grandmother, Mr. Canis (the big bad wolf), and Puck join together to solve mysteries and keep the town in order. "Once Upon a Crime" picks up where book 3 left off. The family takes a very injured Puck to NYC to find his family and has to solve a murder and uncovere more clues about the girls' parents. Many series end up being repetitive after a while (re: the Redwall books), but these have a fresh story for each book.</span>

Do I look like I'm round?"<br /><br />"Sorry," Daphne said, "I didn't mean---"<br /><br />"That kind of ignorance is why gingerbread people are treated so badly all over the world," he said bitterly. <div id="review_99627872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99627872" />
    <a title="Tobey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3202324-tobey"><img alt="Tobey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557327845p2/3202324.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99627872?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tobey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tobey" href="/user/show/3202324-tobey">Tobey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99627872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12348048138342759660">While not really dropping in quality, I felt like the <i>Sisters Grimm</i> series lost a little steam in the fourth book. The mystery was a little more obvious, and the rhythms of the series are becoming a bit more repetitive. Sabrina is going to have an angsty personal problem (learning that her mother was all for fairy tale detecting, which isn't Sabrina's bag) that will be resolved, a mystery must be solved (a murder mystery this time, but the culprit is given away by the cover art), Mr. Canis will </span>
  <span id="freeText12348048138342759660" style="display:none">While not really dropping in quality, I felt like the <i>Sisters Grimm</i> series lost a little steam in the fourth book. The mystery was a little more obvious, and the rhythms of the series are becoming a bit more repetitive. Sabrina is going to have an angsty personal problem (learning that her mother was all for fairy tale detecting, which isn't Sabrina's bag) that will be resolved, a mystery must be solved (a murder mystery this time, but the culprit is given away by the cover art), Mr. Canis will battle with his true self, and Daphne will have a new catchphrase ("Jerkazoid!"). I felt like the author, Buckley, tried to inject a little excitement into this volume with a change of scenery, but leaving Ferryport Landing for New York City actually cut all the tension that's been building in the little town. <br /><br />But when a good series loses a little steam it's not alway the end of the world, and there are still plenty of great moments. I appreciated the respect that existed between Mr. Canis (the Big Bad Wolf) and Sheriff Hamstead (one of the Three Little Pigs), and I liked Mother Goose as a bartender in a bar run by the fairy mafia (fairy godfathers, get it?). And Scrooge as a psychic who can communicate with ghosts was a great idea. Oh, and Long John Silver and Jim Hawkins are now Wall Street pirates who battle Sinbad who captains a New York City ferry. Puck was out of commission for most of the book, and when he shows back up he's <i>slightly</i> more mature.<br /><br />The dark tone is a bit lighter than in the last book, except for a couple of crazy moments. Remember that time when the primary suspect (<b>SPOILER:</b> who didn't actually do it) is straight up executed by being held in front of a freakin' cannon?<br /><br />In summation, it's not the best of the series, but it is still a decent addition.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12348048138342759660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer3906129161461379239">In some ways, this book definitely feels like somewhat of a departure for the series. The story focuses on a different location, there is an incredible focus on an unexpected character, and the book is about revelations that I didn't see coming.<br/><br/>Without going into an incredible amount of detail as to avoid spoilers, Michael Buckley continues to weave a fantastic story using characters in a very clever ways.   <span id="freeText3906129161461379239" style="display:none">In some ways, this book definitely feels like somewhat of a departure for the series. The story focuses on a different location, there is an incredible focus on an unexpected character, and the book is about revelations that I didn't see coming.<br /><br />Without going into an incredible amount of detail as to avoid spoilers, Michael Buckley continues to weave a fantastic story using characters in a very clever ways. There were some bits I didn't LOVE such as all the pirate business, but then there was such insight and character building in other parts of the book that it more than made up for it.<br /><br />I am proud of myself for realizing who the killer was long before it was revealed, however there was another plot point I didn't see coming until moments before it happened.<br /><br />In some ways, this was a book that established a holding pattern and got a bit deeper. I am hoping that Sabrina had a major break through with her character so that she stops being the voice of descent all the time.<br /><br />Also, Michael Buckley seems to be employing the ol' Alias opening that J.J. used so much which makes for an engaging and exciting start to each book.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer100456170" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer183742819204249747">The fourth in a most entertaining fractured-fairy-tale detective series, <i>Once Upon a Crime</i> was a great read. In it, Sabrina and Daphne Grimm & company drive from Ferryport Landing, where most of the Everafters, or fairy-tale characters, live, to New York City, to take the ailing Puck to Faerie so he can be healed by his family (Oberon & Titania and offspring). Turns out Faerie isn't quite what it used to be. The fairy-tale detectives find thuggish fairy godfathers, characters from Oz (the Wizard</span>
  <span id="freeText183742819204249747" style="display:none">The fourth in a most entertaining fractured-fairy-tale detective series, <i>Once Upon a Crime</i> was a great read. In it, Sabrina and Daphne Grimm &amp; company drive from Ferryport Landing, where most of the Everafters, or fairy-tale characters, live, to New York City, to take the ailing Puck to Faerie so he can be healed by his family (Oberon &amp; Titania and offspring). Turns out Faerie isn't quite what it used to be. The fairy-tale detectives find thuggish fairy godfathers, characters from Oz (the Wizard, the Wicked Witch of the West, and we even get a glimpse of the Woggle-Bug), dwarfs in the subway, pirates from Wall Street (one with a parrot who shrieks, "Dump the stock, now! Sell, sell sell!"), and Scrooge (a financial and spiritual adviser) and Tim Cratchit. It was all great fun, and I'm glad there are more of these books to enjoy. </span>

<div id="review_3028777154" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <span id="freeText1952785428707946879" style="display:none">Choice book 4 Quarter 1<br /><br />Book: The Sisters Grimm book 4 - Once Upon Twist is a fantasy book written by Michael Buckley.<br /><br />Setting: This book takes place in Ferryport landing, New York.<br /><br />The main characters: The main characters in the book are Sabrina, Daphne, Puck, Granny Relda, Mr Canis and last but not least Uncle Jake. Sabrina is a 12 year girl that was sent to an orphanage because her parents had mysterious disappeared and now that she is living with her grandmother (Granny Relda) she find out that she is a Grimm and what Grimms do is solve mysterious and not just normal mysterious but mysterious involving Fairy tale characters which they prefer to be identified as everafters. Sabrina also has a little sister named Daphne, Daphne is 7 years old little girl that is loving solving mysterious about everafters. Puck, Puck is a fairy with pink insect-like wings and he like to called himself the all great Trickster King and let me tell you this he is not the cleanest person in the world and he needs to learn manners. He lives with Granny Relda and Sabrina and her sister. Granny Relda is Sabrina and Daphne´s grandmother. They also live with Mr Canis, Mr Canis is the skinniest old man in the world but inside of him lives the beast known as the big bad wolf.<br /><br />The problem/conflict: Puck was attacked by a Jabberwacky and was badly hurt, together with her family Sabrina took him to he´s home town and there he was put in a healing cocoon. Puck was the son of the king of the kingdom which is also puck´s home town, and there the king was poisoned and the Queen (Puck´s mother) went insane. They had to find who poisoned the king and they fought Oz also known was the wonderful wizard of Oz. <br /><br />The plot: Sabrina and Puck were chased by a Jabberwocky and Puck got hurt and was sent to the fairy kingdom and put in a stinky cocoon to heal then after that the king was poisoned and they go on an adventure to find who had poisoned the king. Then they fought Oz to get her mother´s journal back. They also found their parents but they are under a sleeping spell. <br /><br />Opinion and Analysis: I really really liked the book and I think it’s my favorite book of the whole series so far other than the last book I read. (The third book) In one part of the book I almost cried but then I didn’t because it all ended well. My favorite part of the book was all the funny moments with the healing cocoon and Sabrina. This book compared to all the other books I’ve read I think it better than all of them other than this series of course.</span>

The second surprising thing was when everyone realized it was Moth who really killed Oberlin. <div id="review_72920213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72920213" />
    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/981011-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287101719p2/981011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72920213?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi" href="/user/show/981011-mimi">Mimi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/981011-mimi?shelf=older-children">older-children</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72920213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3494619766301266173">I enjoyed this book. I actually guessed way early with this book who the villain would be, way earlier than I usually guess. But I didn't mind, because it is always very satisfying to learn that you are right. I'm trying really hard to guess who "G" is, but you don't have any clues other than she is female and went by the initial "G." I am trying to think of possibly fairy tale maidens. I've thought of Galinda the good witch, Gretel, Guinevere, and dang. I forgot the fourth one I thought of. I'm</span>
  <span id="freeText3494619766301266173" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book. I actually guessed way early with this book who the villain would be, way earlier than I usually guess. But I didn't mind, because it is always very satisfying to learn that you are right. I'm trying really hard to guess who "G" is, but you don't have any clues other than she is female and went by the initial "G." I am trying to think of possibly fairy tale maidens. I've thought of Galinda the good witch, Gretel, Guinevere, and dang. I forgot the fourth one I thought of. I'm sure we'll get more clues in the future.<br /><br />As always, I like how the maturity of Sabrina and Daphne progress.<br /><br />However, I've always been a bit uncomfortable with how their foster parents and the child welfare system are portrayed. Granted, I'm sure some of them are just in it for the money and are unpleasant and abusive, but I would like to think that some foster parents are loving. I would always like to think that our government wouldn't allow someone who had killed seven people to be a foster parent, even if he had already served his time. That little part, these little snippets of evil, just seem to be a little bit much for me in a children's story. The rest of the story is for children, not young adults, so hearing about how evil and abusive the foster parents were always shocks me and makes me a little uncomfortable.<br /><br />However, those mentions are only a few paragraphs out of the whole book, and the rest of the book is very good.<br /><br />I'm interested in where things will go with Puck and Sabrina. He's been a fairy for hundreds of years, so he's technically much older than her, even though as the Trickster King, he's not very mature. She's only eleven though, and he kissed her last book. I think she's too young for a kiss. That's just me though. It was a good fairy tale read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3494619766301266173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37888317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9936068761397282664">When the fairy-tale detectives, Sabrina and Daphne Grimm, rush to New York City hoping to find an Everafter who can cure Puck, they trigger a chain of events that includes a murder mystery, and learn many new things about their mother who, along with their father, is still in an enchanted sleep. The author has created a world in which humans and fairy-tale creatures live side-by-side in an uneasy alliance. Readers, well grounded in their fairy tales, will get the most pleasure from recognizing t</span>
  <span id="freeText9936068761397282664" style="display:none">When the fairy-tale detectives, Sabrina and Daphne Grimm, rush to New York City hoping to find an Everafter who can cure Puck, they trigger a chain of events that includes a murder mystery, and learn many new things about their mother who, along with their father, is still in an enchanted sleep. The author has created a world in which humans and fairy-tale creatures live side-by-side in an uneasy alliance. Readers, well grounded in their fairy tales, will get the most pleasure from recognizing the characters.<br /><br />It is a fast pace story with sly humor, “grown-up” action and cleverly inserted vocabulary lessons aimed squarely at the, newly anointed, Harry Potter/Lemony Snicket market: tween to adult. While I jumped into Book 4, akin to other series, I was given a contextual synopsis of each preceding book and was able to follow the adventure. I would, though, recommend beginning at the beginning, as there is richness and depth of character missing. Sabrina, the sister more heartbroken and wary of the world, is a totally modern “tween”, spouting sass and sarcasm beyond her age. She grapples with the strong desire to be “normal” and accepting her family’s destiny - insert James Earl Jones voice here ;)<br /><br />Interest Level: <br />4th-Adult<br />Age: <br />9yrs+<br />Genre: <br />Fiction<br />Subject: <br />Mystery<br /><br />The Bulletin of the Center for Children’s Books<br />Unexpected meetings and clever conversations between fairy-tale characters …attractive packaging…fans of fractured fairy tales and rollicking adventure will anxiously await the rest of this broadly humorous series.”<br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText7505313082868024107" style="display:none"> I recently read The Sisters Grimm number 4. It was written by Micheal Buckley. It was published in 2007. There are 272 pages. This book is intended for 5th to 9th graders. The main issue is that there trying to figure out who killed Oberon king of fairies.<br /> The setting is New York City. The main characters are Sabrina. She is scared. She has blonde hair and blue eyes. Daphne is 7 years old loves her sister.<br /> Sabrina and Daphne journey to there home town New York City to get puck some help. While they were there Oberon the king of fairies held a party in there honor. While the party was going the king was shot. Now they have to solve the case of who killed Oberon.<br /> I liked how they went back to there hometown. I didn't like how how her mom kept a secret. My favorite quotes are... The little princess shock her head" you don't understand my love. I did this for us. My second quote is.... Puck noticed the goblet lying on the floor. he picked it up and smelled it "now that wasn't very nice" pg 224<br /> The theme is those who mess with the queen are often dead. I recommend this book to those who love fairies. There's a lot of them. The plot was about a fairy. The unique thing about this book is there's a kingdom in New York City. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7505313082868024107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

There's also a few continuity issues that I've noticed, possibly because I'm reading them all so close together. <br/><br/></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ku2Uzx/6uc4LzhW9yA8DPaTWe9ODHRq+CGIiW5Y7BdSQvKoYoRwm0bS7njgAtvFumFDY0oFMBaq5yPmGu96SJw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OtOYeaSJCnC1xTiTiORQEMJ0Ys0y1klwujyvae3Mtuw4gqauGm+VbwqwsxZAXaJD/vLBzDCHVmQLlnS0wCkhHw==')})
  }

With his shape constantly changing, Telmund discovers that actually living in a fairy tale has its drawbacks. Amelia is a practical princess with a wide range of skills, none of which are helpful for escaping the ball her parents have thrown to select her future husband. But then the unthinkable happens: Amelia is kidnapped by the dangerous Prince Sheridan, setting off a plot that will throw the realm into chaos. As their stories become intertwined, the dreamer prince and no-nonsense princess must work together to rescue each other. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3957997760782500237">New York Times bestselling author Michael Buckley was born in Akron, Ohio. He tried his hand as a stand-up comic and lead singer for a punk rock back before attending Ohio University. After graduating with honors he moved to New York City to be an intern on the Late Show with David Letterman which led to stints developing programming for Discovery Networks, MTV, MTV Animation and Klasky Csupo (pro</span>
  <span id="freeText3957997760782500237" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author Michael Buckley was born in Akron, Ohio. He tried his hand as a stand-up comic and lead singer for a punk rock back before attending Ohio University. After graduating with honors he moved to New York City to be an intern on the Late Show with David Letterman which led to stints developing programming for Discovery Networks, MTV, MTV Animation and Klasky Csupo (producers of Nickelodeon’s Rugrats). Today he lives in Brooklyn, New York with his wife, Alison, and their son Finn. <br /><br /><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i> </span>
